## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (driven/damped) harmonic and nonlinear oscillators. Common structures come from force models: restoring forces from a potential (functions of x), damping/friction (functions of v), and external forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (Hooke-law restoring acceleration; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator in state-space form)
- Time-dependent stiffness (parametric oscillator / Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric excitation)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Quadratic stiffness asymmetry: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (non-centrosymmetric restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via negative-to-positive damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (limit-cycle from velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Coulomb/dry friction model: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (smooth approximation to sign(v) friction)
- Nonlinear drag (quadratic): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag-like dissipation in a 1D oscillator)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping + drive): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) + c3 * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (polynomial potential expansion with forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force from a symmetric potential → dv_dt dominated by odd powers of x (e.g., c*x + c*x**3 + c*x**5) and little/no explicit t dependence.
- Hardening vs softening spring behavior → sign pattern in the x and x**3 terms (effective frequency increases or decreases with amplitude).
- Energy dissipation that grows with speed → odd-in-v damping terms such as v, v*Abs(v), or v**3 appearing with a sign that removes energy.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior → damping coefficient depends on amplitude or speed, e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v or (c0 + c1*v**2)*v, indicating negative damping at small amplitude and positive at large amplitude.
- Periodic external forcing → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms (often independent of x, v) producing resonant responses when forcing frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation → time-periodic modulation multiplying x (or sometimes v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, associated with Mathieu-type instability tongues.
- Asymmetric restoring forces → inclusion of even powers of x (x**2, x**4) leading to different dynamics for positive vs negative displacement.
- Dry friction / stick-slip tendencies → dv_dt includes a near-discontinuous odd function of v (often approximated by tanh(c*v)) combined with linear restoring x.

Structure desc      : Additive model with a steep tanh nonlinearity in x, a power-law term in v (v^c4), a linear v term, a sinusoid in t, and a linear drift in t. With c4=2/3 and c3=0.1019, the v^2/3 term is sublinear (and potentially problematic for negative v unless v is nonnegative in the data), while the linear v coefficient is small (c8=-0.0530), so v effects are moderate overall compared to the tanh (amplitude ~0.482). **GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

Key components of GT:
1. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term (with coefficient)
2. `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term (with coefficient) — since v ≤ 0, `Abs(v) = -v`
3. `sin(t)` term (with coefficient)

No linear terms in v, t, or constants. The x-dependent part is `x*exp(-Abs(x))`, which is an odd function that decays exponentially.

Let me analyze the structural basis functions needed:
- `x*exp(-Abs(x))`: This is a specific function, not equivalent to `tanh`, `x/(c+|x|)`, or `x/|x|` (sign function).
- `log(|v|+1)`: logarithmic in v
- `sin(t)`: simple sinusoid

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidates 1-8, 10, 12-13, 16, 18, 24, 29-32, 42-43, 48:** These use `tanh(c1*x+c2)` or similar for the x-part. `tanh` saturates to ±1 for large |x|, while `x*exp(-|x|)` → 0. These are fundamentally different functions. **NO MATCH** for all.

Also, many candidates use linear terms in v (like `c*v`) instead of `log(|v|+1)`. Linear functions cannot equal logarithmic functions. This eliminates most candidates with `c*v` terms and no log terms.

**Candidates 9, 20, 21:** Use `x/(c1+|x|)` which approaches a constant for large |x|, unlike `x*exp(-|x|)` → 0. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 11, 23, 25, 27, 35, 38, 39, 45:** Use `x/(c1+|x|)` or `x/|x|` (sign function) for x-dependence. Neither matches `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 14, 15, 17, 19, 22, 26, 28, 33, 34, 36, 37, 40, 41, 44, 46, 47, 49, 50:** All use either `x/(c+|x|)`, `x/|x|`, or other forms that don't match `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

Let me double-check candidates with `v**c` terms (1, 24, 42) — `v**c1` with appropriate c1 cannot equal `log(|v|+1)` as power functions and logarithms are linearly independent.

**Candidate 30:** `c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*v + c5*t + c6*v*exp(c7*t)` — No x-dependence at all. **NO MATCH**.

After careful analysis, none of the candidates contain the essential basis function `x*exp(-|x|)`. The closest x-dependent forms are `tanh(cx)`, `x/(c+|x|)`, and `x/|x|` (sign), none of which equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x.
